Please provide a value in [0,1] range.\"\n98:         )\n99: \n100:     @torch.no_grad()\n101:     def ema_update(ema_param: Tensor, current_param: Tensor, num_averaged):\n102:         return decay * ema_param + (1 - decay) * current_param\n103: \n104:     return ema_update\n105: \n106: \n107: def get_swa_avg_fn():\n108:     \"\"\"Get the function applying stochastic weight average (SWA) across a single param.\"\"\"\n109: \n110:     @torch.no_grad()\n111:     def swa_update(\n112:         averaged_param: Tensor, current_param: Tensor, num_averaged: Union[Tensor, int]\n113:     ):\n114:         return averaged_param + (current_param - averaged_param) / (num_averaged + 1)\n115: \n116:     return swa_update\n117: \n118: \n119: class AveragedModel(Module):\n120:     r\"\"\"Implements averaged model for Stochastic Weight Averaging (SWA) and Exponential Moving Average (EMA).\n121: \n122:     Stochastic Weight Averaging was proposed in `Averaging Weights Leads to\n123:     Wider Optima and Better Generalization`_ by Pavel Izmailov, Dmitrii\n124:     Podoprikhin, Timur Garipov, Dmitry Vetrov and Andrew Gordon Wilson\n125:     (UAI 2018).\n126: \n127:     Exponential Moving Average is a variation of `Polyak averaging`_,\n128:     but using exponential weights instead of equal weights across iterations.\n129: \n130:     AveragedModel class creates a copy of the provided module :attr:`model`\n131:     on the device :attr:`device` and allows to compute running averages of the\n132:     parameters of the :attr:`model`.\n133: \n134:     Args:\n135:         model (torch.nn.Module): model to use with SWA/EMA\n136:         device (torch.device, optional): if provided, the averaged model will be\n137:             stored on the :attr:`device`\n138:         avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\n139:             parameters; the function must take in the current value of the\n140:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameter, the current value of :attr:`model`\n141:             parameter, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\n142:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\n143:         multi_avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\n144:             parameters inplace; the function must take in the current values of the\n145:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameters as a list, the current values of :attr:`model`\n146:             parameters as a list, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\n147:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\n148:         use_buffers (bool): if ``True``, it will compute running averages for\n149:             both the parameters and the buffers of the model. (default: ``False``)\n150: \n151:     Example:\n152:         >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\"undefined variables\")\n153:         >>> loader, optimizer, model, loss_fn = ...\n154:         >>> swa_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model)\n155:         >>> scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(optimizer,\n156:         >>>                                     T_max=300)\n157:         >>> swa_start = 160\n158:         >>> swa_scheduler = SWALR(optimizer, swa_lr=0.05)\n159:         >>> for i in range(300):\n160:         >>>      for input, target in loader:\n161:         >>>          optimizer.zero_grad()\n162:         >>>          loss_fn(model(input), target).backward()\n163:         >>>          optimizer.step()\n164:         >>>      if i > swa_start:\n165:         >>>          swa_model.update_parameters(model)\n166:         >>>          swa_scheduler.step()\n167:         >>>      else:\n168:         >>>          scheduler.step()\n169:         >>>\n170:         >>> # Update bn statistics for the swa_model at the end\n171:         >>> torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn(loader, swa_model)\n172: \n173:     You can also use custom averaging functions with the `avg_fn` or `multi_avg_fn` parameters.\n174:     If no averaging function is provided, the default is to compute\n175:     equally-weighted average of the weights (SWA).\n176: \n177:     Example:\n178:         >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\"undefined variables\")\n179:         >>> # Compute exponential moving averages of the weights and buffers\n180:         >>> ema_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model,\n181:         >>>             torch.optim.swa_utils.get_ema_multi_avg_fn(0.9), use_buffers=True)\n182: \n183:     .. note::\n184:         When using SWA/EMA with models containing Batch Normalization you may\n185:         need to update the activation statistics for Batch Normalization.\n186:         This can be done either by using the :meth:`torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn`\n187:         or by setting :attr:`use_buffers` to `True`. The first approach updates the\n188:         statistics in a post-training step by passing data through the model. The\n189:         second does it during the parameter update phase by averaging all buffers.\n190:         Empirical evidence has shown that updating the statistics in normalization\n191:         layers increases accuracy, but you may wish to empirically test which\n192:         approach yields the best results in your problem.\n193: \n194:     .. note::\n195:         :attr:`avg_fn` and `multi_avg_fn` are not saved in the :meth:`state_dict` of the model.\n196: \n197:     .. note::\n198:         When :meth:`update_parameters` is called for the first time (i.e.\n199:         :attr:`n_averaged` is `0`) the parameters of `model` are copied\n200:         to the parameters of :class:`AveragedModel`. y) ** 2).mean()\n            loss.backward()\n\n            # Calculate expected variance at this step\n            expected_variance = eta / ((1 + step) ** gamma)\n            variances.append(expected_variance)\n\n            # Perform optimizer step\n            optimizer.step()\n\n            # Reset gradients\n            model.zero_grad()\n\n        # Verify that variances decrease over time\n        for i in range(len(variances) -
